  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_49fa31d4-a996-4157-b426-2e607fda8440'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="review_267861036" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/267861036" />
    <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma"><img alt="Nandakishore Varma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583648733p2/6237864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/267861036?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nandakishore Varma" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma">Nandakishore Varma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/13078003-now-we-are-six">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6237864-nandakishore-varma?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6237864-nandakishore-varma?shelf=children-s-literature">children-s-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267861036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17978447272744148912">Like <i>When We Were Very Young</i>, this is also a terrific compilation. I love it when an adult can see through a child's eyes without losing his "adult-ness". Milne's poetry is simple and beautiful, and his humour can be enjoyed by adults and children alike.<br/><br/>Christopher Robin and Winnie-the-Pooh need no introduction. Quite a few of the poems in this book are about the duo. Milne accomplishes the extraordinary feat of seeing from the realistic and make-believe viewpoint at the same time (something whi</span>
  <span id="freeText17978447272744148912" style="display:none">Like <i>When We Were Very Young</i>, this is also a terrific compilation. I love it when an adult can see through a child's eyes without losing his "adult-ness". Milne's poetry is simple and beautiful, and his humour can be enjoyed by adults and children alike.<br /><br />Christopher Robin and Winnie-the-Pooh need no introduction. Quite a few of the poems in this book are about the duo. Milne accomplishes the extraordinary feat of seeing from the realistic and make-believe viewpoint at the same time (something which comes as second-nature to children, but we lose it as we grow up): therefore, Pooh is a live character to Christopher, even when he knows that he is nothing but a toy (the poem <i>Us Two</i> and <i>The Friend</i>).<br /><br />There are a lot of nonsense poems about silly grownups, quite a few of them kings and emperors, but behaving like spoilt children-a child's view of himself, maybe! (Or a rather uncomfortable thought - is it so childish? Don't dictators behave like spoilt kids on a rampage - with much deadlier results than Milne's characters produce, of course.) There are poignant poems of a child's world which so incomprehensible to adults so that they shoo him away (<i>Come Out With Me</i>). Also, there is the delight only a child can experience, such as a race between two raindrops (<i>Waiting At The Window</i>). There are even profound philosophical questions which plague a young mind (<i>Explained</i>).<br /><br />But for me, the poem which captures the quintessence of childhood in this collection is <i>Buttercup Days</i>, about Anne and her man(!), especially these four lines:<br /><br /><i>What has she got in that little brown head?<br />Wonderful thoughts which can never be said.<br />What has she got in that firm little fist of hers?<br />Somebody's thumb, and it feels like Christopher's.</i><br /><br />Anne and Christopher, among the buttercups. Pure childhood bliss!<br /><br />Five stars, all the way.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="17978447272744148912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_67472751" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67472751" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/135573-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494329995p2/135573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/67472751?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/135573-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer67472751" class="readable"
              >

<div id="review_1742205727" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1742205727" />
    <a title="Rose  Heartfilia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8290245-rose-heartfilia"><img alt="Rose  Heartfilia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540902082p2/8290245.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1742205727?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose  Heartfilia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose  Heartfilia" href="/user/show/8290245-rose-heartfilia">Rose  Heartfilia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780749702083" href="/book/show/1250590.Now_We_Are_Six">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8290245-rose-heartfilia?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8290245-rose-heartfilia?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8290245-rose-heartfilia?shelf=giggle-chuckle-books">giggle-chuckle-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8290245-rose-heartfilia?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1742205727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3913877069709444837">So to make a short story long: a friend of my mother's, his mother died (may she rest in peace). And those people already had a lot of books so all the books of the mother are brought to them and they want to dispose of them, so he calls my mom, asking if I'm interested in books. Me assuming everything was in Dutch, I was not much up to it, but he told me that there were all sorts of books. So well why not, I came there expecting a few boxes with books, maximum up to 3 or so. There were seven of</span>
  <span id="freeText3913877069709444837" style="display:none">So to make a short story long: a friend of my mother's, his mother died (may she rest in peace). And those people already had a lot of books so all the books of the mother are brought to them and they want to dispose of them, so he calls my mom, asking if I'm interested in books. Me assuming everything was in Dutch, I was not much up to it, but he told me that there were all sorts of books. So well why not, I came there expecting a few boxes with books, maximum up to 3 or so. There were seven of them and his wife wasn't allowed to keep any. So it was in the early morning that I spend through seven book boxes to find books I might like, I did like and that I did want to read and since everything would otherwise be gone, some books my friends might want. <br /><br />Thank god I had help from my boyfriend since we didn't have much time, I manage to look through everything and come up with 86 books that I want, a few for my two reading friends and off I could go. One of those books was this one. I am not very familiar with names but as soon as A.A. Milne jumped up I knew it. There has once been a boyfriend of my mother whom collected books (I only liked him because of that of course) and he collected them, Winnie The Pooh stories. I always watched movies when I was a kid. So I was very and am very proud that I have one. I expected a full story written about Winnie but I didn't get that, I got poems which was something else but it was lovely. I didn't get all but I sure did love some of them. I hope to get my hands on a few more, maybe so I can buy them or maybe in the library. Time will tell.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3913877069709444837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_661406773" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/661406773" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50448-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1175789489p2/50448.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/661406773?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/50448-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525479291" href="/book/show/2967962-now-we-are-six">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=2019familytreechallenge">2019familytreechallenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=2019goodrule-old">2019goodrule-old</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=reviewcopy">reviewcopy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=2019reviews">2019reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=readin2013">readin2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=shareatea2019">shareatea2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer661406773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5836212482055207697">First sentence: When you are reciting poetry, which is a thing we never do, you find sometimes, just as you are beginning, that Uncle John is still telling Aunt Rose that if he can't find his spectacles he won't be able to hear properly, and does she know where they are; and by the time everybody has stopped looking for them, you are at the last verse, and in another minute they will be saying, "Thank you, thank you," without really knowing what it was all about.<br/><br/>Premise/plot: This is A.A. Milne'</span>
  <span id="freeText5836212482055207697" style="display:none">First sentence: When you are reciting poetry, which is a thing we never do, you find sometimes, just as you are beginning, that Uncle John is still telling Aunt Rose that if he can't find his spectacles he won't be able to hear properly, and does she know where they are; and by the time everybody has stopped looking for them, you are at the last verse, and in another minute they will be saying, "Thank you, thank you," without really knowing what it was all about.<br /><br />Premise/plot: This is A.A. Milne's second volume of poetry written for children. His first was When We Were Very Young.<br /><br />My thoughts: While I don't absolutely love, love, love Milne's two poetry collections as much as I love his two Pooh novels, I do appreciate them. My favorite poems from Now We Are Six include:<br /><br /> Busy<br /> Binker<br /> Us Two<br /> The Engineer<br /> The End<br /><br />From Busy<br /><br /> I think I am a Muffin Man. I haven't got a bell.<br /> I haven't got the muffin things that muffin people sell.<br /> Perhaps I am a Postman. No, I think I am a Tram.<br /> I'm feeling rather funny and I don't know what I am--<br /> BUT<br /> Round about<br /> And round about<br /> And round about I go--<br /> All around the table,<br /> The table in the nursery--<br /> Round about<br /> And round about<br /> And round about I go;<br /> I think I am a Traveller escaping from a Bear;<br /> I think I am an Elephant,<br /> Behind another Elephant<br /> Behind another Elephant who isn't really there...<br /><br /> From Binker<br /><br /> Binker--what I call him--is a secret of my own,<br /> And Binker is the reason why I never feel alone.<br /> Playing in the nursery, sitting on the stair,<br /> Whatever I am busy at, Binker will be there.<br /> Oh, Daddy is clever, he's a clever sort of man,<br /> And Mummy is the best since the world began,<br /> And Nanny is Nanny, and I call her Nan--<br /> But they can't<br /> See<br /> Binker.<br /><br />From Us Two<br /><br /> Wherever I am, there's always Pooh,<br /> There's always Pooh and Me.<br /> Whatever I do, he wants to do,<br /> "Where are you going today?" says Pooh:<br /> "Well, that's very odd, 'cos I was too.<br /> Let's go together," says Pooh, says he.<br /> "Let's go together," says Pooh.<br /><br /><br />Original audience born circa 1920 to 1924.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5836212482055207697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9694203180645852724">This book is so beautiful with poems and illustrations. I can't help but to smile when I read poems that I can relate to when I was a little kid. Like collecting insects and tadpoles, rooting for a drop of rain on the window to finish 1st, or questioning a lot of silly things. <br/><br/><u>These are my favourites from this collection:</u><br/>1. Solitude<br/>2. Busy <br/>3. Binker <br/>4. Us Two<br/>5. Down by The Pond<br/>6. The Little Black Hen<br/>7. Swing Song<br/>8. Cradle Song<br/>9. Waiting At The Window<br/>10. Wind On The Hill<br/>11. In The Dark<br/>12. The End</span>
  <span id="freeText9694203180645852724" style="display:none">This book is so beautiful with poems and illustrations. Solitude<br />2. Busy <br />3. Binker <br />4. Us Two<br />5. Down by The Pond<br />6. The Little Black Hen<br />7. Swing Song<br />8. Cradle Song<br />9. Waiting At The Window<br />10. Wind On The Hill<br />11. In The Dark<br />12. The End<br /><br /><i>When I was one, <br />I had just begun, <br />when I was two, <br />I was nearly new,<br />When I was three, <br />I was hardly me<br />when I was four, <br />I was not much more, <br />When I was five, <br />I was just alive, <br /><br />But, now I am six, I'm as clever as clever, <br />So I think I'll be six now for ever and ever.</i><br />-The End from Now We Are Six by A.A. Milne.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=family">family</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=nonsense">nonsense</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1426098172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15892977143403520547">This selection, several years after 'When We Were Very Young' is even better. I took a liking to almost all the poems and admired the range of rhythm and rhyme that takes place. Again, Milne plays so much on using the form of poetry to reflect on Christopher's life and adventures and it works so well in terms of there being poems which reflect childhood - a lot like Rosen's early stuff. I'd certainly have a classroom copy and would want to share so many with the class. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2912889295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15617163461209421863">We started reading this at the breakfast table a couple of days after Grayson turned six. The boys loved it. Begging most meals for us to read it, we wouldn’t have gotten past Sneezles if I hadn’t insisted we push on. The giggles were grand and there was a lot of fun. We will have to revisit this every sixth birthday, and maybe more. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2378526961640259606" style="display:none">A wonderful collection of poems about coming of age (if that age is 6). If you enjoyed this, I would highly recommend 'When we were very young' - Milne's other collated verses.</span>

Pooh Bear and company, kinds and queens and nights, Christopher Robin... they all just pop off the page.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2516262436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10658561226041763973">A tiny, tiny book of tiny, tiny poems, filled with lots of rhyme and repetition and delightful silliness. <br/><br/>I was happy to see this little poem that I've used for ages during Poem-in-Your Pocket:<br/><br/>When I was one, I just begun.<br/>When I was two, I was nearly new.<br/>When I was three, I was hardly me.<br/>When I was four,<br/>I was not much more.<br/>When I was five, I was just alive.<br/>But now I’m six,<br/>I'm as clever as clever.<br/>So I think I'll be six now, forever and ever!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OSmeSdqS0u5mcSTk3vSxtIKdP9cpiUjU+Gg6ujQTzVmnEkNDq+oohxFlNpdcHl9/iTAFvM3G1lc+bYs2GLrC4Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

It tells the tale of a hidden home high in the hills. It is discovered one day by a little girl called Lucie, who is in search of her missing pocket handkerchiefs. She knocks on the tiny door, and meets Mrs Tiggy-winkle who does all the washing and ironing for the neighbouring animals. Lucie spends a lovely day helping her, and it\'s only right at the end of the day that she realises Mrs Tiggy-winkle is a hedgehog!\n\nBeatrix Potter is regarded as one of the world\'s best-loved children\'s authors of all time. From her first book, The Tale of Peter Rabbit, published by Frederick Warne in 1902, she went on to create a series of stories based around animal characters including Mrs. Tiggy-winkle, Benjamin Bunny, Jemima Puddle-duck, Mr. Jeremy Fisher and Tom Kitten.\n\nHer humorous, lively tales and beautiful illustrations have become a natural part of childhood. With revenue from the sales of her books, Beatrix Potter bought a farm - Hill Top - in the English Lake District, where she later became a farmer and prize-winning sheep breeder. She launched the now vast merchandise programme by patenting the very first Peter Rabbit doll in 1903. The product range continues to grow today with licences around the world including baby clothing and bedding, nursery decor products and collectables. Upon her death, Beatrix Potter left 14 farms and over 4000 acres of Lake District farmland to the National Trust so that the place that she loved would remain undeveloped and protected for future generations to enjoy.\n\nToday Beatrix Potter\'s original 23 tales are still published by Frederick Warne, alongside a wide range of other formats including baby books, activity books and gift and sound books.\n\nThe Tale of Mrs Tiggy-winkle is number six in Beatrix Potter\'s series of 23 little books.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/81466.A_A_Milne">About A.A. Milne</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/81466.A_A_Milne"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1204664899p3/81466.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/81466.A_A_Milne">A.A. Milne
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,782
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11729467437105356008">Alan Alexander Milne (pronounced /ˈmɪln/) was an English author, best known for his books about the teddy bear Winnie-the-Pooh and for various children's poems. <br/><br/>A. A. Milne was born in Kilburn, London, to parents Vince Milne and Sarah Marie Milne (née Heginbotham) and grew up at Henley House School, 6/7 Mortimer Road (now Crescent), Kilburn, a small public school run by his father. One of his teac</span>
  <span id="freeText11729467437105356008" style="display:none">Alan Alexander Milne (pronounced /ˈmɪln/) was an English author, best known for his books about the teddy bear Winnie-the-Pooh and for various children's poems. <br /><br />A. A. Milne was born in Kilburn, London, to parents Vince Milne and Sarah Marie Milne (née Heginbotham) and grew up at Henley House School, 6/7 Mortimer Road (now Crescent), Kilburn, a small public school run by his father. One of his teachers was H. G. Wells who taught there in 1889–90. Milne attended Westminster School and Trinity College, Cambridge, where he studied on a mathematics scholarship. While there, he edited and wrote for Granta, a student magazine. He collaborated with his brother Kenneth and their articles appeared over the initials AKM. Milne's work came to the attention of the leading British humour magazine Punch, where Milne was to become a contributor and later an assistant editor.<br /> <br />Milne joined the British Army in World War I and served as an officer in the Royal Warwickshire Regiment and later, after a debilitating illness, the Royal Corps of Signals. He was discharged on February 14, 1919.<br /> <br />After the war, he wrote a denunciation of war titled Peace with Honour (1934), which he retracted somewhat with 1940's War with Honour. During World War II, Milne was one of the most prominent critics of English writer P. G. Wodehouse, who was captured at his country home in France by the Nazis and imprisoned for a year. Wodehouse made radio broadcasts about his internment, which were broadcast from Berlin. Although the light-hearted broadcasts made fun of the Germans, Milne accused Wodehouse of committing an act of near treason by cooperating with his country's enemy. Wodehouse got some revenge on his former friend by creating fatuous parodies of the Christopher Robin poems in some of his later stories, and claiming that Milne "was probably jealous of all other writers.... But I loved his stuff."<br /> <br />He married Dorothy "Daphne" de Sélincourt in 1913, and their only son, Christopher Robin Milne, was born in 1920. In 1925, A. A. Milne bought a country home, Cotchford Farm, in Hartfield, East Sussex. During World War II, A. A. Milne was Captain of the Home Guard in Hartfield &amp; Forest Row, insisting on being plain 'Mr. Milne' to the members of his platoon. He retired to the farm after a stroke and brain surgery in 1952 left him an invalid and by August 1953 "he seemed very old and disenchanted".<br /><br />He was 74 years old when he passed away in 1956.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11729467437105356008" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

  <!--
This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
